## 告别(別)
---
## say goodbye to; part from
### gàobié
---
- **traditional:** 告別
- **definition:** say goodbye to; part from
- **pinyin:** gàobié
- **components:**
  - 告
    - gào
    - inform; announce; tell
  - 别(別)
    - bié
    - leave; part; farewell; separate
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:**
    - 告 (gào, "inform") + 别(別) (bié, "leave; part") =
    - say goodbye; farewell
  - **interpretation:** The word 告别(別) (gàobié, "say goodbye; farewell") consists of 告 (gào, "inform") and 别(別) (bié, "leave; part"). When you 'inform' someone about a 'parting,' you are essentially saying goodbye. This concept is relevant in both personal departures and formal farewells.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)告别(別)。
    - Wǒmen gàobié.
    - We say farewell.
  - 他在码(碼)头(頭)告别(別)，依依不舍地离(離)去。
    - Tā zài mǎtóu gàobié, yīyī bùshě dì líqù.
    - He said farewell at the dock and left reluctantly.
  - 朋友聚会(會)后(後)告别，彼此期待重逢。
    - Péngyǒu jùhuì hòu gàobié, bǐcǐ qídài chóngféng.
    - After the gathering, friends said farewell, each looking forward to reuniting.
### 告别(別) → 告
- **definition:** inform; announce; tell
- **pinyin:** gào
- **components:**
  - 壴
    - zhù
    - drum
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 初 (chū, 'initial') depiction unclear ->
    - later interpretations consider abbreviated 壴 (zhù, 'drum') + 口 (kǒu, 'mouth') =
    - drum with open mouth ->
    - 'announce, tell'
  - **interpretation:** The character 告 (gào, 'inform; announce; tell') likely evolved from a depiction related to announcing or informing others using a combination of sound (drum) and speech (mouth). The interpretation of 告 as a drum and mouth aligns with its meaning of announcing or speaking out loud.
- **examples:**
  - 老师(師)告学(學)生，考试(試)规(規)则(則)已更新。
    - Lǎoshī gào xuéshēng, kǎoshì guīzé yǐ gēngxīn.
    - The teacher informed the students that the exam rules have been updated.
  - 父亲(親)告我，晚上早點回家。
    - Fùqīn gào wǒ, wǎnshàng zǎodiǎn huí jiā.
    - My father informed me to come home early tonight.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 告](@media/glyph544a.png)
### 告别(別) → 告 → 壴
- **definition:** drum
- **pinyin:** zhù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a drum 壴, with a base and feathers 土 on top ->
    - stylized in the Kangxi radical 鼓
  - **interpretation:** The character 壴 (zhù, "drum") visually represents a drum with two ends, with elements contributing to its structure, such as a base and feathers. It was later incorporated into characters like 鼓 (gǔ, "drum") by adding elements that illustrate additional actions like hands holding a drumstick.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)面壴声(聲)震天动(動)地。
    - Zhè miàn zhù shēng zhèn tiān dòng dì.
    - The sound of this drum shakes the heavens and the earth.
  - 战(戰)士敲响(響)壴，示警敌(敵)人。
    - Zhànshì qiāo xiǎng zhù, shì jǐng dírén.
    - The soldier beats the drum to warn the enemy.
  - 庄(莊)严(嚴)仪(儀)式上，祭司击(擊)打壴，宣告传(傳)统(統)。
    - Zhuāngyán yíshì shàng, jìsī jī dǎ zhù, xuānguò chuántǒng.
    - At the solemn ceremony, the priest beats the drum to proclaim tradition.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 壴](@media/glyph58f4.png)
### 告别(別) → 告 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 口](@media/glyph53e3.png)
### 告别(別) → 别(別)
- **traditional:** 別
- **definition:** leave; part; farewell; separate
- **pinyin:** bié
- **components:**
  - 冎
    - guǎ
    - bone
  - 刂(刀)
    - dāo
    - knife
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 冎 ('bone') + 刂 ('knife') =
    - to cut up bone and flesh ->
    - 別
  - **interpretation:** The character originally depicted using a knife to cut up bone and flesh, symbolizing separation. This intuition leads to meanings like 'to part' or 'to separate,' reflecting the act of dividing or moving away from something or someone.
  - **simplification:** The traditional character 別 was directly retained in its simplified form without further reduction in strokes.
- **examples:**
  - 请(請)别(別)担(擔)心。
    - Qǐng bié dānxīn.
    - Please don't worry.
  - 我们(們)在车(車)站告别(別)，他渐(漸)渐(漸)走远(遠)。
    - Wǒmen zài chēzhàn gàobié, tā jiànjiàn zǒu yuǎn.
    - We said goodbye at the station, and he gradually walked away.
  - 他别(別)开(開)旧(舊)生活，开(開)始新的冒险(險)。
    - Tā bié kāi jiù shēnghuó, kāishǐ xīn de màoxiǎn.
    - He left his old life and started a new adventure.
### 告别(別) → 别(別) → 冎
- **definition:** bone
- **pinyin:** guǎ
- **components:**
  - 骨
    - gǔ
    - bone
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts bones ->
    - original form of 骨 (gǔ, "bone")
  - **interpretation:** The character 冎 is a pictogram representing bones and serves as the original form of 骨 (gǔ, "bone"). Its depiction captures the outline of bones, highlighting its usage in ancient scripts. It also appears in other characters as a component, maintaining its essence related to structure and form.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)个(個)汉(漢)字由偏旁和冎构(構)成，其中冎提供了语(語)音线(線)索。
    - Zhège hànzì yóu piānpáng hé guǒ gòuchéng, qízhōng guǒ tígōng le yǔyīn xiànsuǒ.
    - This character is composed of radicals and guǒ, wherein guǒ provides a phonetic clue.
  - 在古代造字过(過)程中，冎常作为(為)声(聲)旁使用。
    - Zài gǔdài zàozì guòchéng zhōng, guǒ cháng zuòwéi shēngpáng shǐyòng.
    - In the process of character creation in ancient times, guǒ was often used as a phonetic component.
  - 冎是一种(種)发(發)音提示符。
    - Guǒ shì yī zhǒng fāyīn tíshì fú.
    - Guǒ is a phonetic indicator.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 冎](@media/glyph518e.png)
### 告别(別) → 别(別) → 冎 → 骨
- **definition:** bone
- **pinyin:** gǔ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts the human spine and ribs, resembling a skeletal structure.
  - **interpretation:** The character 骨 (gǔ, "bone") visually represents the shape and layout of a human spine and ribs.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)根骨很坚(堅)硬。
    - Zhè gēn gǔ hěn jiānyìng.
    - This bone is very hard.
  - 老中医(醫)观(觀)察骨的脉(脈)络(絡)，寻(尋)找健康之秘。
    - Lǎo zhōngyī guānchá gǔ de màiluò, xúnzhǎo jiànkāng zhī mì.
    - The experienced Chinese doctor examines the bone structure to seek the secret of health.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 骨](@media/glyph9aa8.png)
### 告别(別) → 别(別) → 刂
- **definition:** knife
- **pinyin:** dāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** Variant of 刀 ( dāo ).
  - **description:**
    - 刁 (diāo, "clever") is a variant of 刀 (dāo, "knife") ->
    - simplification for clarity
  - **interpretation:** The character 刂(dāo) is a simplified variant of 刀(dāo), which is a pictogram depicting a knife. The two-stroke 刂(dāo) is often used as a radical in other characters related to cutting or knives. It maintains the core meaning and functionality of 刀(dāo) in a more streamlined form.
  - **simplification:** 刂(dāo) is a cursive shorthand of 刀(dāo), used as a radical for clarity and conciseness in compound characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他用刂(刀)，迅速劈开(開)木头(頭)。
    - Tā yòng dāo, xùnsù pī kāi mùtou.
    - He uses a knife to quickly chop wood.
  - 厨房里挂着一把闪亮的刂(刀)，让(讓)人看了食欲(慾)大增。
    - Chúfáng lǐ guà zhe yī bǎ shǎnliàng de dāo, ràng rén kàn le shíyù dà zēng.
    - A shining knife hangs in the kitchen, arousing one's appetite.
  - 刂(刀)是厨(廚)房中不可缺少的工具。
    - Dāo shì chúfáng zhōng bùkě quēshǎo de gōngjù.
    - The knife is an indispensable tool in the kitchen.

## 飞(飛)吻
---
## kiss one's hand to; blow a kiss
### fēiwěn
---
- **traditional:** 飛吻
- **definition:** kiss one's hand to; blow a kiss
- **pinyin:** fēiwěn
- **components:**
  - 飞(飛)
    - fēi
    - fly; swift; floating in air
  - 吻
    - wěn
    - kiss; lips; mouth
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** The word 飛吻 (fēiwěn) is composed of 飛 (fēi, "fly") and 吻 (wěn, "kiss").
  - **interpretation:** 飛 (fēi, "fly") denotes motion through the air, ideal for expressing something that travels without physical contact. 吻 (wěn, "kiss") involves the lips or the act of kissing. Together, they depict a kiss that is 'sent through the air,' which naturally captures the idea of blowing a kiss or sending a kiss gesture without touch.
- **examples:**
  - 她向舞台(臺)上的演员(員)送了一个(個)飞(飛)吻。
    - Tā xiàng wǔtái shàng de yǎnyuán sòngle yí ge fēiwěn.
    - She blew a kiss to the actor on the stage.
  - 小女孩给(給)她的妈(媽)妈(媽)送了一个(個)飞(飛)吻。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái gěi tā de māma sòngle yí ge fēiwěn.
    - The little girl blew a kiss to her mom.
  - 在告别(別)的时(時)候，他用力送了个(個)飞(飛)吻。
    - Zài gàobié de shíhou, tā yònglì sòngle ge fēiwěn.
    - When saying goodbye, he blew a vigorous kiss.
### 飞(飛)吻 → 飞(飛)
- **traditional:** 飛
- **definition:** fly; swift; floating in air
- **pinyin:** fēi
- **components:**
  - 升
    - shēng
    - ascend
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a bird flying upwards ->
    - modern form resembles a tasseled 升 (shēng, "ascend")
  - **interpretation:** The traditional form 飛(fēi, "fly") originally depicted a bird ascending, capturing the essence of flight. This reflects its meaning as visualized through the image of the flying bird.
  - **simplification:** The simplified form 飞(fēi, "fly") streamlines the depiction by reducing the strokes of the flying bird while still capturing the essence of flight to convey its meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 鸟(鳥)在天空中飞(飛)翔。
    - Niǎo zài tiānkōng zhōng fēixiáng.
    - The bird is flying in the sky.
  - 他梦(夢)想着(著)有一天能飞(飛)上蓝(藍)天。
    - Tā mèngxiǎngzhe yǒu yītiān néng fēi shàng lántiān.
    - He dreams of flying up to the blue sky one day.
  - 飞(飛)机(機)在云(雲)层(層)间(間)快速飞(飛)行。
    - Fēijī zài yúncéng jiān kuàisù fēixíng.
    - The plane flies quickly between the clouds.
### 飞(飛)吻 → 飞(飛) → 升
- **definition:** ascend
- **pinyin:** shēng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a dipper ->
    - used to represent volume or measure
  - **interpretation:** The character 升(shēng, 'rise') originally depicted a measuring device, like a dipper, used for rice or liquids, emphasizing its function related to measurement or capacity.
- **examples:**
  - 太阳(陽)升起了。
    - Tàiyáng shēngqǐ le.
    - The sun has risen.
  - 太阳(陽)缓(緩)缓(緩)升起，照亮大地。
    - Tàiyáng huǎn huǎn shēngqǐ, zhàoliàng dàdì.
    - The sun slowly rises, illuminating the earth.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 升](@media/glyph5347.png)
### 飞(飛)吻 → 吻
- **definition:** kiss; lips; mouth
- **pinyin:** wěn
- **components:**
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
  - 勿
    - wù
    - do not
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 口 (kǒu, "mouth") + phonetic 勿 (wù) ->
    - meaning
  - **interpretation:** 口 (kǒu, "mouth") suggests the action involves the mouth, which is central to the act of a kiss. The character 勿 (wù) provides the sound. There is no direct semantic contribution from 勿 beyond its phonetic value.
- **examples:**
  - 她给(給)了我一个(個)温(溫)柔的吻。
    - Tā gěile wǒ yīgè wēnróu de wěn.
    - She gave me a gentle kiss.
  - 他们(們)在月光下接吻。
    - Tāmen zài yuèguāng xià jiēwěn.
    - They kissed under the moonlight.
  - 初吻总(總)是让(讓)人难(難)以忘怀(懷)。
    - Chūwěn zǒng shì ràng rén nányǐ wànghuái.
    - The first kiss is always unforgettable.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 吻](@media/glyph543b.png)
### 飞(飛)吻 → 吻 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 口](@media/glyph53e3.png)
### 飞(飛)吻 → 吻 → 勿
- **definition:** do not
- **pinyin:** wù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts blood on a knife ->
    - original character of 刎 (wěn, "to cut") ->
    - jiajie for 勿 (wù, "do not")
  - **interpretation:** The character 勿(wù), originally illustrated blood on a knife, visually represented the action of cutting, connecting to its initial meaning. Over time, it was borrowed to express prohibition or negation, showing the evolution beyond its pictorial roots.
- **examples:**
  - 进(進)入图(圖)书(書)馆(館)时(時)，请(請)勿大声(聲)喧哗(嘩)。
    - Jìnrù túshūguǎn shí, qǐng wù dàshēng xuānhuá.
    - When entering the library, please do not speak loudly.
  - 办(辦)公区(區)内(內)勿吸烟(煙)。
    - Bàngōng qū nèi wù xīyān.
    - Do not smoke in the office area.
  - 行路时(時)，勿追逐打闹(鬧)。
    - Xínglù shí, wù zhuīzhú dǎnào.
    - When walking, do not engage in chasing and rough play.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 勿](@media/glyph52ff.png)

## 刚(剛)刚(剛)
---
## just; no more than
### gānggāng
---
- **traditional:** 剛剛
- **definition:** just; no more than
- **pinyin:** gānggāng
- **components:**
  - 刚(剛)
    - gāng
    - just; firm
  - 刚(剛)
    - gāng
    - just; firm
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 刚(剛) (gāng, "just; firm") + 刚(剛) (gāng, "just; firm") reinforce the sense of immediacy or recent occurrence.
  - **interpretation:** The repetition of 刚(剛) (gāng, "just; firm") emphasizes the idea of something having happened very recently or just moments before. This concept is reflected in its common use to indicate 'just now' or 'just recently' in time expressions. The doubling intensifies the immediacy.
- **examples:**
  - 他刚(剛)刚(剛)走。
    - Tā gānggāng zǒu.
    - He just left.
  - 我刚(剛)刚(剛)到了，看到朋友站在门(門)外。
    - Wǒ gānggāng dào le, kàn dào péngyǒu zhàn zài ménwài.
    - I just arrived and saw a friend standing outside the door.
### 刚(剛)刚(剛) → 刚(剛)
- **traditional:** 剛
- **definition:** just; firm
- **pinyin:** gāng
- **components:**
  - 岡
    - gāng
    - mountain ridge
  - 刀
    - dāo
    - knife
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 岡 (gāng) + semantic 刀 (knife) ->
    - hard, firm
  - **interpretation:** 岡 (gāng, 'mountain ridge') provides the sound, suggesting a firm or solid structure, with 刀 (dāo, 'knife') indicating sharpness or firmness. Thus, 刚(剛) (gāng, 'firm') connotes hardness or strength, while the definite, exact nature of a firm edge lends to meanings of precise timing ('just now') and minimal sufficiency ('barely').
  - **simplification:** 剛 (gāng, 'firm') was simplified to 刚(剛) by replacing the phonetic 岡 (gāng, 'mountain ridge') with 冈, retaining the knife radical 刀.
- **examples:**
  - 我刚(剛)吃完晚饭(飯)。
    - Wǒ gāng chī wán wǎnfàn.
    - I just finished dinner.
  - 他刚(剛)走进(進)教室，铃(鈴)声(聲)就响(響)了。
    - Tā gāng zǒu jìn jiàoshì, língshēng jiù xiǎng le.
    - He just entered the classroom when the bell rang.
  - 这(這)个(個)盒子很坚(堅)硬，像石头(頭)一样(樣)。
    - Zhège hézi hěn jiānyìng, xiàng shítou yīyàng.
    - This box is very hard, like a stone.
### 刚(剛)刚(剛) → 刚(剛) → 岡
- **definition:** mountain ridge
- **pinyin:** gāng
- **components:**
  - 网(網)
    - mǎng
    - net
  - 山
    - shān
    - mountain
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 网 (mǎng) + semantic 山 (shān, "mountain") ->
    - ridge
  - **interpretation:** The character combines the semantic 山 (shān, "mountain") suggesting a topographical feature, with the phonetic 网 (mǎng) to provide the sound. A ridge is a prominent mountain feature, making this combination intuitive for indicating 'ridge'.
- **examples:**
  - 那座高冈(岡)，是徒步旅行的好地方。
    - Nà zuò gāo gāng, shì túbù lǚxíng de hǎo dìfāng.
    - That high ridge is a great place for hiking.
  - 太阳(陽)从(從)山冈(岡)升起，洒(灑)下金色的光芒。
    - Tàiyáng cóng shān gāng shēng qǐ, sǎ xià jīnsè de guāngmáng.
    - The sun rises from the ridge, casting golden rays.
  - 在冈(岡)顶(頂)上，你可以看到整个(個)村庄(莊)。
    - Zài gāng dǐng shàng, nǐ kěyǐ kàn dào zhěnggè cūnzhuāng.
    - On the top of the ridge, you can see the entire village.
### 刚(剛)刚(剛) → 刚(剛) → 岡 → 网(網)
- **traditional:** 網
- **definition:** net
- **pinyin:** mǎng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a net with crossing lines or mesh ->
    - symbol for 'net'
  - **interpretation:** The character 网(網) (wǎng, 'net') visually represents a net with lines intersecting to form a grid, making it intuitive as a symbol for a net or mesh.
  - **simplification:** The simplified character 网 (wǎng) retains the essential visual structure of intersecting lines to depict a net. It conveys the idea of a net through a simplified representation without additional semantic or phonetic elements.
- **examples:**
  - 他用网(網)捕鱼(魚)，快乐(樂)满(滿)怀(懷)。
    - Tā yòng wǎng bǔ yú, kuàilè mǎn huái.
    - He fishes with a net and is full of joy.
  - 很多信息通过(過)网(網)传(傳)播，速度惊(驚)人。
    - Hěn duō xìnxī tōngguò wǎng chuánbō, sùdù jīngrén.
    - A lot of information spreads through the net with astonishing speed.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 网](@media/glyph7f51.png)
### 刚(剛)刚(剛) → 刚(剛) → 岡 → 山
- **definition:** mountain
- **pinyin:** shān
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts three mountain peaks
  - **interpretation:** The character 山(shān, "mountain") visually represents the concept of a mountain using three vertical lines that suggest peaks. This depiction is consistent with early forms found in Oracle Bone Script, emphasizing the notion of natural elevation associated with mountains.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)去爬山。
    - Wǒmen qù pá shān.
    - We go climb the mountain.
  - 那座大山让(讓)人惊(驚)叹(嘆)。
    - Nà zuò dà shān ràng rén jīngtàn.
    - That mountain astonishes people.
  - 远(遠)处(處)的山隐(隱)约(約)在云(雲)中，令人心旷(曠)神怡。
    - Yuǎnchù de shān yǐnyuē zài yún zhōng, lìng rén xīnkuàng shényí.
    - The distant mountain fades into the clouds, leaving one in a state of peace.

### 刚(剛)刚(剛) → 刚(剛) → 刀
- **definition:** knife
- **pinyin:** dāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a knife
  - **interpretation:** 刀 (dāo, "knife") is a pictographic representation of a knife or blade, with a sharp edge and a handle, resembling the form of a basic cutting tool.
- **examples:**
  - 他用锋(鋒)利的刀，切开(開)蔬菜。
    - tā yòng fēnglì de dāo, qiē kāi shūcài.
    - He uses a sharp knife to cut vegetables.
  - 这(這)把刀非常锋(鋒)利。
    - zhè bǎ dāo fēicháng fēnglì.
    - This knife is very sharp.
  - 厨(廚)师(師)小心地持刀，为(為)客人切肉。
    - chúshī xiǎoxīn de chí dāo, wèi kèrén qiē ròu.
    - The chef holds the knife carefully and slices meat for the guest.

## 爱(愛)情
---
## love (between a man and a woman)
### àiqíng
---
- **traditional:** 愛情
- **definition:** love (between a man and a woman)
- **pinyin:** àiqíng
- **components:**
  - 爱(愛)
    - ài
    - love
  - 情
    - qíng
    - emotion; sentiment; feeling
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 愛 (ài, "love") as affection or deep feeling, and 情 (qíng, "emotion; sentiment") as emotional state or sentiment, together denote romantic feelings.
  - **interpretation:** 愛 (ài, "love") illustrates deep attachment and commitment, which is the foundation of a romantic bond. 情 (qíng, "emotion; sentiment") captures the subjective, often passionate, feelings between partners. Together, 愛情 (àiqíng) emphasizes romantic love, characterized by both commitment and passionate emotional connection.
- **examples:**
  - 爱(愛)情是我们(們)生活中的一部分。
    - Àiqíng shì wǒmen shēnghuó zhōng de yī bùfèn.
    - Love is a part of our lives.
  - 在电(電)影里(裡)，爱(愛)情总(總)是充满(滿)挑战(戰)。
    - Zài diànyǐng lǐ, àiqíng zǒng shì chōngmǎn tiǎozhàn.
    - In movies, love is always full of challenges.
  - 他的小说(說)里(裡)描述了很多种(種)爱(愛)情。
    - Tā de xiǎoshuō lǐ miáoshù le hěn duō zhǒng àiqíng.
    - His novels describe many types of love.
### 爱(愛)情 → 爱(愛)
- **traditional:** 愛
- **definition:** love
- **pinyin:** ài
- **components:**
  - 旡
    - jì
    - none
  - 心
    - xīn
    - heart
  - 夊
    - suī
    - foot
  - 友
    - yǒu
    - friend
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - 旡 (phonetic) + 心 (heart) ->
    - 㤅; 夊 (foot) added ->
    - 𢙴; top 旡 corrupted to ⿱爫冖 ->
    - 愛
  - **interpretation:** The original form 㤅 combined the phonetic element 旡 with the semantic component 心 (heart), symbolizing the emotional nature of love. To depict the involvement of people, the redundant component 夊 (foot) was later added, changing the form to 𢙴. Over time, the top phonetic component 旡 was transformed into ⿱爫冖, resulting in the current character 愛, which continues to convey the concept of love from the heart, with nuances of involving or interacting with others.
  - **simplification:** The lower component of 愛, 夊, was replaced with 友 (yǒu, "friend") in the simplified form 爱 to reduce strokes while retaining a conceptually related element.
- **examples:**
  - 她的微笑让(讓)我感到温(溫)暖和爱(愛)。
    - Tā de wēixiào ràng wǒ gǎndào wēnnuǎn hé ài.
    - Her smile fills me with warmth and love.
  - 父母总(總)是无(無)条(條)件地爱(愛)我们(們)。
    - Fùmǔ zǒng shì wú tiáojiàn dì ài wǒmen.
    - Parents always love us unconditionally.
  - 爱(愛)是人生中最重要的情感。
    - Ài shì rénshēng zhōng zuì zhòngyào de qínggǎn.
    - Love is the most important emotion in life.
### 爱(愛)情 → 爱(愛) → 旡
- **definition:** none
- **pinyin:** jì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a kneeling figure turning around with mouth open
  - **interpretation:** The character 旡(jì, 'inhale') represents a pictogram depicting a kneeling figure with an open mouth, suggesting the action of inhaling. This form is visually distinct as it shows a figure turning with mouth open, akin to inhaling deeply.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 旡](@media/glyph65e1.png)
### 爱(愛)情 → 爱(愛) → 心
- **definition:** heart
- **pinyin:** xīn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a heart
  - **interpretation:** The character 心(xīn, "heart") originally depicted the shape of an actual heart, representing thoughts, emotions, and the core of a person. Over time, it has become highly stylized, but it continues to convey the notion of the heart as the center of emotions and consciousness.
- **examples:**
  - 她的心一直都在帮(幫)助别(別)人。
    - Tā de xīn yīzhí dōu zài bāngzhù biérén.
    - Her heart is always in helping others.
  - 在城市的中心，有一个(個)美丽(麗)的公园(園)。
    - Zài chéngshì de zhōngxīn, yǒu yí gè měilì de gōngyuán.
    - At the center of the city, there is a beautiful park.
  - 对(對)于(於)许(許)多人来(來)说(說)，家庭是生活的核心。
    - Duìyú xǔduō rén lái shuō, jiātíng shì shēnghuó de héxīn.
    - For many people, family is the core of life.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 心](@media/glyph5fc3.png)
### 爱(愛)情 → 爱(愛) → 夊
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** suī
- **components:**
  - 夂
    - zhǐ
    - to go
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a footprint pointing downward; variant of 夂 (zhǐ, "to go")
  - **interpretation:** The character 夊(suī, "downward foot") visually represents a downward-facing foot, suggesting movement or trajectory in a downward direction.
- **examples:**
  - 他的步伐缓(緩)慢，就像夊一般。
    - Tā de bùfá huǎnmàn, jiù xiàng suī yībān.
    - His steps are slow, like the character 夊.
  - 我们(們)观(觀)察到古代文字中，常常使用夊来(來)表达(達)脚(腳)的动(動)作。
    - Wǒmen guānchá dào gǔdài wénzì zhōng, chángcháng shǐyòng suī lái biǎodá jiǎo de dòngzuò.
    - We observed that in ancient texts, the character 夊 was often used to express the action of the foot.
- **historical forms:**

### 爱(愛)情 → 爱(愛) → 夊 → 夂
- **definition:** to go
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a footprint pointing down
  - **interpretation:** The character 夂 (zhǐ, 'foot pointing down') is a pictogram representing a footprint facing downward, often associated with motion or directionality. This depiction intuitively aligns with its meaning of indicating a downward step or path.
- **examples:**
  - 汉(漢)字中‘夂’常被用作偏旁，象征(徵)步伐朝下。
    - Hànzì zhōng ‘zhǐ’ cháng bèi yòng zuò piān páng, xiàng zhēng bù fá cháo xià.
    - In Chinese characters, '夂' is often used as a radical to symbolize downward steps.
  - 书(書)法中‘夂’的结(結)构(構)犹(猶)如足尖向下。
    - Shūfǎ zhōng ‘zhǐ’ de jiégòu yóurú zújiān xiàng xià.
    - In calligraphy, the structure of '夂' resembles a foot pointing downward.

### 爱(愛)情 → 爱(愛) → 友
- **definition:** friend
- **pinyin:** yǒu
- **components:**
  - 又
    - yòu
    - again
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 又 (yòu, 'again') + phonetic 又 (yòu, 'again') ->
    - mutual reaching out ->
    - friendship
  - **interpretation:** The character 友 (yǒu, 'friend') depicts two iterations of 又 (yòu, 'again'), stylized to suggest two hands reaching towards each other, symbolizing mutual support and assistance fundamental to friendship.
- **examples:**
  - 我们(們)是好朋友。
    - Wǒmen shì hǎo péngyǒu.
    - We are good friends.
  - 她喜欢(歡)和朋友一起去旅行。
    - Tā xǐhuān hé péngyǒu yīqǐ qù lǚxíng.
    - She likes to travel with friends.
  - 每个(個)人都需要朋友的支持。
    - Měi gèrén dōu xūyào péngyǒu de zhīchí.
    - Everyone needs the support of friends.

### 爱(愛)情 → 爱(愛) → 友 → 又
- **definition:** again
- **pinyin:** yòu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a right hand
  - **interpretation:** The character 又 (yòu, "hand") is a pictogram representing a right hand, showing the fingers and palm, which highlights its original meaning related to manual actions.
- **examples:**
  - 「又」这(這)个(個)字最早来(來)源于(於)手。
    - 「Yòu」 zhè gè zì zuì zǎo láiyuán yú shǒu。
    - The character '又' originally comes from the hand.
  - 很多汉(漢)字含有又部首，表示与(與)手有关(關)的动(動)作。
    - Hěn duō hànzì hányǒu Yòu bùshǒu, biǎoshì yǔ shǒu yǒuguān de dòngzuò。
    - Many Chinese characters include the '又' radical, indicating actions related to the hand.
  - 古人用又描绘(繪)手的形态(態)，体(體)现(現)了古汉(漢)字的独(獨)特魅力。
    - Gǔrén yòng Yòu miáohuì shǒu de xíngtài, tǐxiàn le gǔ hànzì de dútè mèilì。
    - Ancient people used '又' to depict the shape of the hand, showcasing the unique charm of ancient Chinese characters.
- **historical forms:**

### 爱(愛)情 → 情
- **definition:** emotion; sentiment; feeling
- **pinyin:** qíng
- **components:**
  - 心
    - xīn
    - heart
  - 青
    - qīng
    - green; young
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 心 (xīn, "heart") + phonetic 青 (qīng) ->
    - emotions; feelings
  - **interpretation:** The character 情(qíng) combines the semantic component 心 (xīn, "heart"), representing emotions and feelings, with the phonetic component 青 (qīng) to suggest the pronunciation. The heart is considered the seat of emotions, thus naturally leading to the character's meaning of "emotions; feelings."
- **examples:**
  - 他的情感非常丰(豐)富。
    - Tā de qínggǎn fēicháng fēngfù.
    - His emotions are very rich.
  - 她对(對)这(這)部电(電)影没(沒)有任何情感。
    - Tā duì zhè bù diànyǐng méiyǒu rènhé qínggǎn.
    - She has no feelings towards this movie.
  - 在写(寫)信时(時)，表达(達)自己的情感很重要。
    - Zài xiě xìn shí, biǎodá zìjǐ de qínggǎn hěn zhòngyào.
    - When writing a letter, it's important to express one's emotions.
### 爱(愛)情 → 情 → 心
- **definition:** heart
- **pinyin:** xīn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a heart
  - **interpretation:** The character 心(xīn, "heart") originally depicted the shape of an actual heart, representing thoughts, emotions, and the core of a person. Over time, it has become highly stylized, but it continues to convey the notion of the heart as the center of emotions and consciousness.
- **examples:**
  - 她的心一直都在帮(幫)助别(別)人。
    - Tā de xīn yīzhí dōu zài bāngzhù biérén.
    - Her heart is always in helping others.
  - 在城市的中心，有一个(個)美丽(麗)的公园(園)。
    - Zài chéngshì de zhōngxīn, yǒu yí gè měilì de gōngyuán.
    - At the center of the city, there is a beautiful park.
  - 对(對)于(於)许(許)多人来(來)说(說)，家庭是生活的核心。
    - Duìyú xǔduō rén lái shuō, jiātíng shì shēnghuó de héxīn.
    - For many people, family is the core of life.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 心](@media/glyph5fc3.png)
### 爱(愛)情 → 情 → 青
- **definition:** green; young
- **pinyin:** qīng
- **components:**
  - 生
    - shēng
    - life
  - 井
    - jǐng
    - well
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 生 (shēng, "life") + phonetic 井 (jǐng, "well") ->
    - final form
  - **interpretation:** The character 青(qīng, "green") originally combines the phonetic components 生(shēng, "life") and 井(jǐng, "well") for their sound values. The ancient interpretation associated 青(qīng) with the color of growing plants, possibly influenced by the idea of cinnabar for dyeing, reflecting a bluish-green shade common in nature. This phonetic pairing with 生 and 井 suggests a pronunciation that fits the word's meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 树(樹)叶(葉)是青色的。
    - Shùyè shì qīngsè de.
    - The leaves are green.
  - 青山环(環)绕(繞)着(著)村庄(莊)。
    - Qīngshān huánrào zhe cūnzhuāng.
    - Green hills surround the village.
  - 她有一双(雙)青色的眼睛。
    - Tā yǒu yī shuāng qīngsè de yǎnjīng.
    - She has a pair of green eyes.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 青](@media/glyph9752.png)
### 爱(愛)情 → 情 → 青 → 生
- **definition:** life
- **pinyin:** shēng
- **components:**
  - 屮
    - chè
    - sprout
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 屮 (chè, "sprout") on top of a horizontal line ->
    - signifies a plant sprouting from the ground ->
    - symbolizes life
  - **interpretation:** The character 生 (shēng, "life") represents the concept of life force or vitality, symbolized by a sprout emerging from the earth, embodying growth and renewal.
- **examples:**
  - 生命是一场(場)美丽(麗)的旅程。
    - Shēngmìng shì yī chǎng měilì de lǚchéng.
    - Life is a beautiful journey.
  - 他在战(戰)场(場)上奋(奮)力生存。
    - Tā zài zhànchǎng shàng fènlì shēngcún.
    - He fights to live on the battlefield.
  - 这(這)家餐厅(廳)的生鱼(魚)片非常新鲜(鮮)。
    - Zhè jiā cāntīng de shēngyúpiàn fēicháng xīnxiān.
    - The raw fish slices at this restaurant are very fresh.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 生](@media/glyph751f.png)
### 爱(愛)情 → 情 → 青 → 生 → 屮
- **definition:** sprout
- **pinyin:** chè
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a sprout emerging from the ground
  - **interpretation:** 屮 (chè, 'sprout') is a pictogram that directly represents a young plant or sprout emerging from the ground. Its visual form captures the essence of new growth, and it historically served as an early representation of plant life or new vegetation.
- **examples:**
  - 春雨滋润(潤)后(後)，小屮冲(沖)破泥土而出。
    - chūn yǔ zī rùn hòu, xiǎo chè chōng pò ní tǔ ér chū.
    - After the spring rain nurtured the earth, the little sprout broke through the soil.
  - 草屮初生露尖端。
    - cǎo chè chū shēng lù jiān duān.
    - The grass sprout's tip has just emerged.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 屮](@media/glyph5c6e.png)
### 爱(愛)情 → 情 → 青 → 井
- **definition:** well
- **pinyin:** jǐng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a grid symbolizing a well's structure
  - **interpretation:** The character 井 (jǐng, "well") visually represents the framework or grid of wooden or stone beams that would make up the top view of a traditional well, highlighting its function and design.
- **examples:**
  - 村口有一口老井。
    - Cūnkǒu yǒuyī kǒu lǎo jǐng.
    - There is an old well at the village entrance.
  - 夏天酷热(熱)时(時)，井水带(帶)来(來)阵(陣)阵(陣)凉(涼)意。
    - Xiàtiān kùrè shí, jǐng shuǐ dàilái zhèn zhèn liángyì.
    - In the scorching summer, well water brings a refreshing coolness.
- **historical forms:**

## 并(並)
---
## used before a negative for emphasis, usu. as a retort
### bìng
---
- **traditional:** 並
- **definition:** used before a negative for emphasis, usu. as a retort
- **pinyin:** bìng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Originally depicted two people standing side-by-side ->
    - representing alignment or togetherness
  - **interpretation:** The character 並 originally depicted two individuals standing next to each other, emphasizing the concept of being together or aligned, which relates directly to its meaning of combined action or inclusivity.
  - **simplification:** The character 并 simplifies 並 by reducing the repetition of strokes representing two people to a single form, conveying the same meaning through a straightforward design.
- **examples:**
  - 他并(並)不是不想去参(參)加聚会(會)。
    - Tā bìng bù shì bù xiǎng qù cānjiā jùhuì.
    - He doesn't actually not want to attend the party.
  - 我并(並)不觉(覺)得这(這)个(個)问(問)题(題)很复(複)杂(雜)。
    - Wǒ bìng bù juéde zhège wèntí hěn fùzá.
    - I don't think this problem is complicated at all.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 并](@media/glyph5e76.png)

## 往事
---
## bygones; past events
### wǎngshì
---
- **definition:** bygones; past events
- **pinyin:** wǎngshì
- **components:**
  - 往
    - wǎng
    - past; toward
  - 事
    - shì
    - affair; event; matter
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 往 (wǎng, "past; toward") refers to the direction of going away, or the time that has passed, emphasizing what has been and is no more. 事 (shì, "affair; event; matter") denotes occurrences or activities. Thus, 往事 (wǎngshì, "bygones; past events") combines these elements to refer to events or matters of the past.
  - **interpretation:** The word 往事 (wǎngshì, "bygones; past events") captures the sense of looking back at the 'affairs or events' (事) that belong to the 'past' (往). Anything that once occurred is considered a 'past event,' emphasizing the separation between then and now.
- **examples:**
  - 他常常回忆(憶)往事。
    - Tā chángcháng huíyì wǎngshì.
    - He often reminisces about past events.
  - 记(記)住往事，才能更好地走向未来(來)。
    - Jìzhu wǎngshì, cáinéng gèng hǎo de zǒuxiàng wèilái.
    - Remembering the past helps to better move towards the future.
  - 往事已成过(過)眼云(雲)烟(煙)。
    - Wǎngshì yǐ chéng guòyǎn yúnyān.
    - Past events have already become fleeting clouds.
### 往事 → 往
- **definition:** past; toward
- **pinyin:** wǎng
- **components:**
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 彳
    - chì
    - step
  - 王
    - wáng
    - king
  - 主
    - zhǔ
    - lord
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - Originally 止 (zhǐ, "foot") + 王 (wáng, "king") =
    - phonetic for pronunciation ->
    - 彳 (chì, "step") added for movement ->
    - right component stylized to unrelated 主 (zhǔ, "lord") forming final character
  - **interpretation:** The character 往(wǎng) incorporates semantic and phonetic elements: 彳(chì, "step") suggests movement and 止(zhǐ, "foot") indicates direction, while 王(wáng, "king") originally provided the pronunciation, which was later obscured as the character evolved.
- **examples:**
  - 他往门(門)口走。
    - Tā wǎng ménkǒu zǒu.
    - He walked towards the door.
  - 我们(們)往东(東)边(邊)旅行。
    - Wǒmen wǎng dōngbian lǚxíng.
    - We are traveling east.
  - 她常常回忆(憶)往事。
    - Tā chángcháng huíyì wǎngshì.
    - She often reminisces about the past.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 往](@media/glyph5f80.png)
### 往事 → 往 → 止
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 趾
    - zhǐ
    - foot
  - 龰
    - yù
    - stylized feet
  - 手
    - shǒu
    - hand
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Original: Foot pointing up with 3 toes and a sole ->
    - Stylized as 龰 ->
    - Derivative 趾 refers to original 'foot' meaning
  - **interpretation:** Originally depicting a footprint with toes and a sole, 止 (zhǐ, "foot") represents the foot. The character's form resembles a foot with three toes, analogous to how the hand is represented with fingers in other characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)的止需要静(靜)养(養)。
    - Tā shòu shāng de zhǐ xū yào jìng yǎng.
    - His injured foot needs adequate rest.
  - 他走路时(時)小心谨(謹)慎，因为(爲)止若受伤(傷)便难(難)前行。
    - Tā zǒu lù shí xiǎo xīn jǐn shèn, yīn wèi zhǐ ruò shòu shāng biàn nán qián xíng.
    - He walks carefully because if his foot gets injured, it becomes difficult to move forward.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 止](@media/glyph6b62.png)
### 往事 → 往 → 止 → 趾
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zhǐ
- **components:**
  - 足
    - zú
    - foot
  - 止
    - zhǐ
    - halt
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 足 (zú, "foot") + phonetic 止 (zhǐ) ->
    - toe
  - **interpretation:** The character combines 足 (zú, "foot"), indicating the general area involved, with 止 (zhǐ) providing the sound and potentially suggesting the idea of a part of the foot that 'halts' or 'stops' progression, which naturally leads to the notion of a toe.
- **examples:**
  - 他的脚(腳)趾受伤(傷)了。
    - Tā de jiǎozhǐ shòushāng le.
    - His toe is injured.
  - 她用脚(腳)趾轻(輕)轻(輕)地踢了一下球。
    - Tā yòng jiǎozhǐ qīngqīng de tī le yīxià qiú.
    - She gently kicked the ball with her toe.
  - 在沙滩(灘)上散步时(時)，我感受到沙子在我的脚(腳)趾间(間)流动(動)。
    - Zài shātān shàng sànbù shí, wǒ gǎnshòu dào shāzi zài wǒ de jiǎozhǐ jiān liúdòng.
    - While walking on the beach, I felt the sand flowing between my toes.
### 往事 → 往 → 止 → 趾 → 足
- **definition:** foot
- **pinyin:** zú
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a leg ->
    - originally depicted as ⽦ ->
    - represents 'foot'
  - **interpretation:** The character 足(zú, 'foot') is a pictographic representation of a human leg, which directly portrays the concept of a 'foot'. The pictographic origin emphasizes its fundamental meaning in the language.
- **examples:**
  - 他受伤(傷)后(後)，他的足不能动(動)。
    - tā shòushāng hòu, tā de zú bù néng dòng。
    - After he was injured, his foot couldn't move.
  - 小明打球时(時)，不小心扭伤(傷)了足。
    - xiǎo míng dǎ qiú shí, bù xiǎoxīn niǔ shāng le zú。
    - When Xiaoming was playing ball, he accidentally twisted his foot.
  - 我每天锻(鍛)炼(鍊)足部。
    - wǒ měitiān duànliàn zúbù。
    - I exercise my foot muscles every day.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 足](@media/glyph8db3.png)
### 往事 → 往 → 止 → 龰
- **definition:** stylized feet
- **pinyin:** yù
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts a stylized footprint pointing upward ->
    - originally meaning 'foot' ->
    - later forms like 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') refer back to original meaning
  - **interpretation:** 龰 (yù, 'stylized feet') is a pictogram showing a footprint pointing up, originally indicating the concept of a foot. The character 趾 (zhǐ, 'toe') evolved from this and retains the reference to the original meaning. It visually resembles a sole with three toes, similar to representations of the human hand in characters like 爪 (zhuǎ, 'claw'), 寸 (cùn, 'inch'), and 又 (yòu, 'again').
### 往事 → 往 → 止 → 手
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** shǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a hand with fingers; top stroke is a bent over middle finger, horizontal strokes represent fingers
  - **interpretation:** The character 手 (shǒu, "hand") is a direct pictorial representation of a human hand with all five fingers, which distinguishes it from similar characters representing claws or simplified fingers. This visually conveys its meaning as a hand clearly.
- **examples:**
  - 他用手写(寫)字。
    - Tā yòng shǒu xiě zì.
    - He writes with his hand.
  - 妈(媽)妈(媽)牵(牽)着(著)我的手走路。
    - Māmā qiān zhe wǒ de shǒu zǒu lù.
    - Mom holds my hand while walking.
  - 他的手很温(溫)暖，带(帶)给(給)我力量。
    - Tā de shǒu hěn wēn nuǎn, dài gěi wǒ lìliàng.
    - His hand is very warm, giving me strength.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 手](@media/glyph624b.png)
### 往事 → 往 → 彳
- **definition:** step
- **pinyin:** chì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a foot or person walking
  - **interpretation:** 彳(chì, 'walking') visually represents steps or a person moving, suggesting the idea of walking or movement. Despite a simplified history from characters like 行(xíng, 'walk'), its pictographic heritage directly connects with the notion of stepping or proceeding.
- **examples:**
  - 他喜欢(歡)在河边(邊)慢慢地走。
    - Tā xǐhuān zài hé biān mànmàn de zǒu.
    - He likes to walk slowly by the river.
  - 我们(們)每天退出喧嚣(囂)，享受安静(靜)的散步。
    - Wǒmen měitiān tuìchū xuānxiāo, xiǎngshòu ānjìng de sànbù.
    - We withdraw from the hustle and bustle every day to enjoy a quiet walk.
  - 他常常独(獨)自彳亍于(於)公园(園)小径(徑)。
    - Tā chángcháng dúzì chìchù yú gōngyuán xiǎojìng.
    - He often walks alone on the park trails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 彳](@media/glyph5f73.png)
### 往事 → 往 → 王
- **definition:** king
- **pinyin:** wáng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a ritual axe representing the king's authority
  - **interpretation:** This character represents the form of a ceremonial axe, which was the symbol of a king's power in ancient China. The structure emphasizes the sacred and authoritative role of the king, separate from the nuanced folk interpretations linking Heaven, Man, and Earth.
- **examples:**
  - 他被称(稱)为(為)王，领(領)导(導)人民。
    - Tā bèi chēng wéi wáng, lǐngdǎo rénmín.
    - He is called the king, leading his people.
  - 古代的君主常被尊称(稱)为(為)王。
    - Gǔdài de jūnzhǔ cháng bèi zūnchēng wéi wáng.
    - Ancient rulers were often respectfully called kings.
  - 在祭祀仪(儀)式上，人们(們)向王致敬。
    - Zài jìsì yíshì shàng, rénmen xiàng wáng zhìjìng.
    - During the ceremonial sacrifices, people salute the king.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 王](@media/glyph738b.png)
### 往事 → 往 → 主
- **definition:** lord
- **pinyin:** zhǔ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a torch with a flame on top, symbolizing guidance or leadership
  - **interpretation:** The character 主 (zhǔ, "master") represents a torch with a flame, symbolizing a guiding or leading figure, akin to a master or lord providing direction.
- **examples:**
  - 他是我们(們)家的主。
    - Tā shì wǒmen jiā de zhǔ.
    - He is the master of our family.
  - 僧侣(侶)虔诚(誠)祷(禱)告主。
    - Sēnglǚ qiánchéng dǎogào zhǔ.
    - The monks devoutly prayed to the Lord.
  - 臣子忠心辅(輔)佐主。
    - Chénzi zhōngxīn fǔzuǒ zhǔ.
    - The ministers loyally assist their master.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 主](@media/glyph4e3b.png)
### 往事 → 事
- **definition:** affair; event; matter
- **pinyin:** shì
- **components:**
  - 又
    - yòu
    - hand
  - 中
    - zhōng
    - a flagpole with a drum
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 又 (yòu, "hand") + 中 (zhōng, "a flagpole with a drum") =
    - flag in hand ->
    - to perform one's job
  - **interpretation:** The character 事 (shì, "matter") represents the concept of handling or managing affairs, symbolized by holding a flag, indicating a formal duty or role. The flagpole with a drum suggests organized activity or official matters.
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)件事很复(複)杂(雜)。
    - Zhè jiàn shì hěn fùzá.
    - This matter is very complicated.
  - 小事也能引发(發)大问(問)题(題)，我们(們)需要认(認)真对(對)待。
    - Xiǎo shì yě néng yǐn fā dà wèntí, wǒmen xūyào rènzhēn duìdài.
    - Even small matters can trigger big problems; we need to handle them seriously.
  - 他总(總)是处(處)理各种(種)事，不管大小。
    - Tā zǒng shì chǔlǐ gèzhǒng shì, bùguǎn dàxiǎo.
    - He always manages various affairs, regardless of their significance.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 事](@media/glyph4e8b.png)
### 往事 → 事 → 又
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** yòu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a right hand
  - **interpretation:** The character 又 (yòu, "hand") is a pictogram representing a right hand, showing the fingers and palm, which highlights its original meaning related to manual actions.
- **examples:**
  - 「又」这(這)个(個)字最早来(來)源于(於)手。
    - 「Yòu」 zhè gè zì zuì zǎo láiyuán yú shǒu。
    - The character '又' originally comes from the hand.
  - 很多汉(漢)字含有又部首，表示与(與)手有关(關)的动(動)作。
    - Hěn duō hànzì hányǒu Yòu bùshǒu, biǎoshì yǔ shǒu yǒuguān de dòngzuò。
    - Many Chinese characters include the '又' radical, indicating actions related to the hand.
  - 古人用又描绘(繪)手的形态(態)，体(體)现(現)了古汉(漢)字的独(獨)特魅力。
    - Gǔrén yòng Yòu miáohuì shǒu de xíngtài, tǐxiàn le gǔ hànzì de dútè mèilì。
    - Ancient people used '又' to depict the shape of the hand, showcasing the unique charm of ancient Chinese characters.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 又](@media/glyph53c8.png)
### 往事 → 事 → 中
- **definition:** a flagpole with a drum
- **pinyin:** zhōng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an arrow piercing through the center of a target
  - **interpretation:** The character 中 (zhōng, "middle") visually represents an arrow passing through the central point of a target, illustrating the concept of 'center' or 'middle' effectively. This visual imagery is straightforward and memorable, corresponding closely with its meaning of being at the center or middle of something.
- **examples:**
  - 他站在道路中，看着(著)远(遠)方。
    - tā zhàn zài dàolù zhōng, kànzhe yuǎnfāng.
    - He stands in the middle of the road, gazing into the distance.
  - 房间(間)正中，挂(掛)着(著)一幅名画(畫)。
    - fángjiān zhèng zhōng, guàzhe yī fú mínghuà.
    - A famous painting hangs in the exact center of the room.
- **historical forms:**

## 初恋(戀)
---
## first love
### chūliàn
---
- **traditional:** 初戀
- **definition:** first love
- **pinyin:** chūliàn
- **components:**
  - 初
    - chū
    - beginning; first
  - 恋(戀)
    - liàn
    - love; long for
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 初 (chū, "beginning; first") + 恋(戀) (liàn, "love; long for")
  - **interpretation:** 初 (chū, "beginning; first") indicates the earliest or first instance of something, establishing the context of 'firstness'. 恋(戀) (liàn, "love; long for") expresses the emotion of deep affection or desire. Together, 初戀 (chūliàn, "first love") suggests the initial experience of love or romantic feelings in a person's life.
- **examples:**
  - 他的初恋(戀)是一位邻(鄰)居家的女孩。
    - Tā de chūliàn shì yī wèi línjū jiā de nǚhái.
    - His first love was a girl from the neighbor's house.
  - 初恋(戀)的回忆(憶)总(總)是最甜美。
    - Chūliàn de huíyì zǒng shì zuì tiánměi.
    - The memories of first love are always the sweetest.
  - 我在十五岁(歲)时(時)遇到我的初恋(戀)。
    - Wǒ zài shíwǔ suì shí yùdào wǒ de chūliàn.
    - I met my first love when I was fifteen.
### 初恋(戀) → 初
- **definition:** beginning; first
- **pinyin:** chū
- **components:**
  - 衤
    - yī
    - clothes
  - 刀
    - dāo
    - knife
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 衤 ('clothes') + 刀 ('knife') =
    - starting by cutting fabric ->
    - initial, beginning
  - **interpretation:** When beginning to make clothing, one starts by cutting the cloth. This initial action represents the concept of 'beginning' or 'initial'. The character visually conveys the combination of these two elements: a piece of fabric and the act of cutting, which together symbolize the starting point of creating clothing.
- **examples:**
  - 在学(學)习(習)的初期，我花了很多时(時)间(間)阅(閱)读(讀)课(課)本。
    - Zài xuéxí de chūqī, wǒ huā le hěn duō shíjiān yuèdú kèběn.
    - In the initial stages of studying, I spent a lot of time reading textbooks.
  - 初夏时(時)节(節)，花儿(兒)们(們)纷(紛)纷(紛)绽(綻)放。
    - Chūxià shíjié, huā'érmen fēnfēn zhànfàng.
    - In early summer, the flowers bloom abundantly.
  - 我们(們)在旅程的开(開)端充满(滿)期待。
    - Wǒmen zài lǚchéng de kāiduān chōngmǎn qídài.
    - At the beginning of the journey, we are filled with anticipation.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 初](@media/glyph521d.png)
### 初恋(戀) → 初 → 衤
- **definition:** clothes
- **pinyin:** yī
- **components:**
  - 衣
    - yī
    - clothing
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 衤(left radical form of 衣 (yī, "clothing")) ->
    - version of 衣 showing depiction of folded or worn garment
  - **interpretation:** 衤 is a variant form of 衣 (yī, "clothing"), representing the appearance of a folded or worn garment, used when part of other characters where the focus is related to clothing or garments.
- **examples:**
  - 他穿上一件新衤。
    - Tā chuānshàng yī jiàn xīn yī.
    - He put on a new outfit.
  - 衤字象征(徵)着(著)人的外表。
    - Yī zì xiàngzhēngzhe rén de wàibiǎo.
    - The character 衤 symbolizes the appearance of a person.
  - 古代的衤主要用来(來)遮盖(蓋)身体(體)。
    - Gǔdài de yī zhǔyào yòng lái zhē gài shēntǐ.
    - In ancient times, clothing was mainly used to cover the body.
### 初恋(戀) → 初 → 衤 → 衣
- **definition:** clothing
- **pinyin:** yī
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a basic outline of a garment with sleeves hanging down.
  - **interpretation:** The character 衣 (yī, 'clothes') clearly resembles a simple garment, with parts representing sleeves and the body of clothing. This visual representation aligns with its meaning of 'clothes' or 'clothing.'
- **examples:**
  - 这(這)件衣很特别(別)。
    - Zhè jiàn yī hěn tè bié.
    - This piece of clothing is very special.
  - 冬天来(來)了，人们(們)换(換)上了暖和的衣。
    - Dōngtiān lái le, rénmen huàn shàng le nuǎn huó de yī.
    - Winter has arrived, and people put on warm clothes.

### 初恋(戀) → 初 → 刀
- **definition:** knife
- **pinyin:** dāo
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a knife
  - **interpretation:** 刀 (dāo, "knife") is a pictographic representation of a knife or blade, with a sharp edge and a handle, resembling the form of a basic cutting tool.
- **examples:**
  - 他用锋(鋒)利的刀，切开(開)蔬菜。
    - tā yòng fēnglì de dāo, qiē kāi shūcài.
    - He uses a sharp knife to cut vegetables.
  - 这(這)把刀非常锋(鋒)利。
    - zhè bǎ dāo fēicháng fēnglì.
    - This knife is very sharp.
  - 厨(廚)师(師)小心地持刀，为(為)客人切肉。
    - chúshī xiǎoxīn de chí dāo, wèi kèrén qiē ròu.
    - The chef holds the knife carefully and slices meat for the guest.

### 初恋(戀) → 恋(戀)
- **traditional:** 戀
- **definition:** love; long for
- **pinyin:** liàn
- **components:**
  - 䜌
    - lì
    - various, miscellaneous
  - 心
    - xīn
    - heart
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - phonetic 䜌 + semantic 心 ('heart') ->
    - ties of the heart ->
    - romance
  - **interpretation:** 戀(lì) represents 'romance' by combining 心(xīn, 'heart') as the semantic element indicating emotions, with 䜌 as the phonetic component suggesting the sound 'liàn'. The heart tied up or entangled captures the sense of romantic attachment and longing.
  - **simplification:** 戀 was simplified to 恋(戀) by removing the phonetic 䜌 and retaining only the semantic 心(xīn, 'heart').
- **examples:**
  - 他们(們)的恋(戀)情很浪漫。
    - Tāmen de liànqíng hěn làngmàn.
    - Their romance is very romantic.
  - 她在校园(園)里(裡)与(與)他相恋(戀)。
    - Tā zài xiàoyuán lǐ yǔ tā xiāngliàn.
    - She fell in love with him on campus.
  - 他一直希望找到一份真诚(誠)的爱(愛)情。
    - Tā yīzhí xīwàng zhǎodào yī fèn zhēnchéng de àiqíng.
    - He has always hoped to find a sincere love.
### 初恋(戀) → 恋(戀) → 䜌
- **definition:** various, miscellaneous
- **pinyin:** lì
- **components:**
  - 糸
    - sī
    - silk; thread
  - 言
    - yán
    - speech
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogrammic compound
  - **description:**
    - 糸 (sī, "silk; thread") + 言 (yán, "speech") =
    - threads of speech ->
    - various, miscellaneous
  - **interpretation:** The combination of 糸 (sī, "silk; thread") with 言 (yán, "speech") suggests speech that is woven together in various threads, representing a collection of different and miscellaneous topics or narratives.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 䜌](@media/glyph470c.png)
### 初恋(戀) → 恋(戀) → 䜌 → 糸
- **definition:** silk; thread
- **pinyin:** sī
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a skein of silk
  - **interpretation:** The character 糸(mì, "silk; thread") represents a pictorial representation of a skein of silk, visually capturing the concept of thread or fiber.
- **examples:**
  - 她手工制(製)作了一条(條)漂亮的丝(絲)巾。
    - Tā shǒugōng zhìzuòle yī tiáo piàoliang de sī jīn.
    - She handcrafted a beautiful silk scarf.
  - 这(這)个(個)设(設)计(計)图(圖)必须(須)用细(細)糸画(畫)出来(來)。
    - Zhège shèjìtú bìxū yòng xì mì huà chūlái.
    - This design drawing must be sketched with fine thread.
  - 我们(們)参(參)观(觀)了古代的织(織)布技术(術)，对(對)丝(絲)绸(綢)制(製)作产(產)生了兴(興)趣。
    - Wǒmen cānguānle gǔdài de zhībù jìshù, duì sīchóu zhìzuò chǎnshēngle xìngqù.
    - We visited ancient weaving techniques and developed an interest in silk production.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 糸](@media/glyph7cf8.png)
### 初恋(戀) → 恋(戀) → 䜌 → 言
- **definition:** speech
- **pinyin:** yán
- **components:**
  - 舌
    - shé
    - tongue
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** ideogram
  - **description:**
    - 舌 (mouth with a forked tongue) with added stroke at top to suggest tongue movement ->
    - speech
  - **interpretation:** The character 言(yán, "speech") depicts the addition of a horizontal stroke to the ancient form of 舌(shé, "tongue") to indicate the motion of the tongue as it moves to articulate speech. This directly connects the organ involved in speaking to the concept of speech itself.
- **examples:**
  - 他的言语(語)充满(滿)智慧。
    - Tā de yányǔ chōngmǎn zhìhuì.
    - His speech is full of wisdom.
  - 我们(們)应(應)该(該)以行动(動)证(證)明我们(們)的言词(詞)。
    - Wǒmen yīnggāi yǐ xíngdòng zhèngmíng wǒmen de yáncí.
    - We should prove our words with actions.
  - 他说(說)话(話)的方式显(顯)示了他的修养(養)。
    - Tā shuōhuà de fāngshì xiǎnshìle tā de xiūyǎng.
    - The way he speaks shows his refinement.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 言](@media/glyph8a00.png)
### 初恋(戀) → 恋(戀) → 䜌 → 言 → 舌
- **definition:** tongue
- **pinyin:** shé
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a forked tongue emerging upwards from a mouth
  - **interpretation:** The character 舌(shé, 'tongue') visually represents a tongue extending out from a mouth, which aligns with its meaning. This direct depiction makes it easy to remember its association with speech and taste in its semantic family, also relating to words like 言(yán, 'word').
- **examples:**
  - 他的舌非常灵(靈)敏。
    - Tā de shé fēicháng língmǐn.
    - His tongue is very sensitive.
  - 品尝(嚐)美食时(時)，他的舌细(細)品滋味。
    - Pǐncháng měishí shí, tā de shé xì pǐn zīwèi.
    - While tasting delicious food, his tongue savors every flavor.
  - 他长(長)舌无(無)忌，经(經)常泄露秘密。
    - Tā chángshé wújì, jīngcháng xièlòu mìmì.
    - He is talkative and often spills secrets.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 舌](@media/glyph820c.png)
### 初恋(戀) → 恋(戀) → 䜌 → 言 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 口](@media/glyph53e3.png)
### 初恋(戀) → 恋(戀) → 心
- **definition:** heart
- **pinyin:** xīn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a heart
  - **interpretation:** The character 心(xīn, "heart") originally depicted the shape of an actual heart, representing thoughts, emotions, and the core of a person. Over time, it has become highly stylized, but it continues to convey the notion of the heart as the center of emotions and consciousness.
- **examples:**
  - 她的心一直都在帮(幫)助别(別)人。
    - Tā de xīn yīzhí dōu zài bāngzhù biérén.
    - Her heart is always in helping others.
  - 在城市的中心，有一个(個)美丽(麗)的公园(園)。
    - Zài chéngshì de zhōngxīn, yǒu yí gè měilì de gōngyuán.
    - At the center of the city, there is a beautiful park.
  - 对(對)于(於)许(許)多人来(來)说(說)，家庭是生活的核心。
    - Duìyú xǔduō rén lái shuō, jiātíng shì shēnghuó de héxīn.
    - For many people, family is the core of life.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 心](@media/glyph5fc3.png)

## 活
---
## live; be alive
### huó
---
- **definition:** live; be alive
- **pinyin:** huó
- **components:**
  - 氵(水)
    - shuǐ
    - water
  - 舌
    - shé
    - tongue
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - 氵(水, "water") + 𠯑 (phonetic) transformed to 舌(舌, "tongue") =
    - life-giving water ->
    - live; be alive
  - **interpretation:** The character 活 (huó, "live; be alive") symbolizes the essential role of water 氵(水) in sustaining life, enhanced by the phonetic component initially represented by 𠯑 but later transformed into 舌(舌, "tongue"). This reflects how water is crucial for vitality and life.
- **examples:**
  - 他活得很快乐(樂)。
    - Tā huó de hěn kuàilè.
    - He lives very happily.
  - 人们(們)需要水才能活。
    - Rénmen xūyào shuǐ cáinéng huó.
    - People need water to live.
  - 如果努力工作，我们(們)会(會)活得更好。
    - Rúguǒ nǔlì gōngzuò, wǒmen huì huó de gèng hǎo.
    - If we work hard, we will live better.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 活](@media/glyph6d3b.png)
### 活 → 氵
- **definition:** water
- **pinyin:** shuǐ
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - 氵is the radical form of 水 (shuǐ, "water") ->
    - depicts flowing water, compressed and stylized next to characters.
  - **interpretation:** The character 氵is a simplified variant used as a radical to represent water-related meanings in other characters. It retains the flowing water depiction of 水 (shuǐ, "water") but is stylized to fit alongside other components.
- **examples:**
  - 水是生命之源。
    - Shuǐ shì shēngmìng zhī yuán.
    - Water is the source of life.
  - 汉(漢)字中偏旁氵，代表水。
    - Hànzì zhōng piān páng shuǐ, dàibiǎo shuǐ.
    - In Chinese characters, the radical '氵' signifies water.
  - 河水清澈透明，鱼(魚)儿(兒)欢(歡)快戏(戲)水。
    - Hé shuǐ qīngchè tòumíng, yú er huānkuaì xì shuǐ.
    - The river water is clear and transparent, and the fish happily play in it.
### 活 → 舌
- **definition:** tongue
- **pinyin:** shé
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a forked tongue emerging upwards from a mouth
  - **interpretation:** The character 舌(shé, 'tongue') visually represents a tongue extending out from a mouth, which aligns with its meaning. This direct depiction makes it easy to remember its association with speech and taste in its semantic family, also relating to words like 言(yán, 'word').
- **examples:**
  - 他的舌非常灵(靈)敏。
    - Tā de shé fēicháng língmǐn.
    - His tongue is very sensitive.
  - 品尝(嚐)美食时(時)，他的舌细(細)品滋味。
    - Pǐncháng měishí shí, tā de shé xì pǐn zīwèi.
    - While tasting delicious food, his tongue savors every flavor.
  - 他长(長)舌无(無)忌，经(經)常泄露秘密。
    - Tā chángshé wújì, jīngcháng xièlòu mìmì.
    - He is talkative and often spills secrets.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 舌](@media/glyph820c.png)

## 打听(聽)
---
## ask about; inquire about
### dǎtīng
---
- **traditional:** 打聽
- **definition:** ask about; inquire about
- **pinyin:** dǎtīng
- **components:**
  - 打
    - dǎ
    - hit; make; break; strike
  - 聽
    - tīng
    - listen; hear
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** 打 (dǎ, "hit") originally means to strike or hit, but it has extended meanings such as to make or to carry out an action. 聽 (tīng, "listen") means to listen or hear. Together, 打聽 (dǎtīng) conveys the idea of actively seeking information by listening and asking questions.
  - **interpretation:** The combination of 打 (dǎ, "hit") and 聽 (tīng, "listen") suggests the proactive act of gathering information by listening and inquiring. It implies engaging others to listen to their replies while inquiring.
- **examples:**
  - 她在打听(聽)一个(個)朋友的消息。
    - Tā zài dǎtīng yī gè péngyǒu de xiāoxi.
    - She is inquiring about a friend's news.
  - 他总(總)是喜欢(歡)打听(聽)别(別)人的私事。
    - Tā zǒngshì xǐhuān dǎtīng biérén de sīshì.
    - He always likes to ask about other people's private matters.
  - 我去市场(場)打听(聽)水果的价(價)格，发(發)现(現)苹(蘋)果很便宜。
    - Wǒ qù shìchǎng dǎtīng shuǐguǒ de jiàgé, fāxiàn píngguǒ hěn piányí.
    - I went to the market to inquire about the price of fruits and found that apples are very cheap.
### 打听(聽) → 打
- **definition:** hit; make; break; strike
- **pinyin:** dǎ
- **components:**
  - 扌
    - shǒu
    - hand
  - 丁
    - dīng
    - fourth; robust
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - 扌 (shǒu, "hand") + 丁 (dīng) =
    - action involving the hand with a phonetic element ->
    - to hit or strike
  - **interpretation:** The character 打(dǎ) combines the semantic element "hand" 扌, suggesting an action performed by hand, with the phonetic element 丁(dīng), which indicates the pronunciation. This composition reflects the basic meaning of 'to hit' or 'strike'.
- **examples:**
  - 他在运(運)动(動)会(會)上打破了世界纪(紀)录(錄)。
    - Tā zài yùndònghuì shàng dǎpòle shìjiè jìlù.
    - He broke the world record at the sports meet.
  - 我打电(電)话(話)给(給)朋友。
    - Wǒ dǎ diànhuà gěi péngyǒu.
    - I am calling a friend.
  - 他们(們)喜欢(歡)在空地上打篮(籃)球。
    - Tāmen xǐhuān zài kòngdì shàng dǎ lánqiú.
    - They like to play basketball on the open ground.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 打](@media/glyph6253.png)
### 打听(聽) → 打 → 扌
- **definition:** hand
- **pinyin:** shǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a stylized hand. The top stroke is the bent middle finger, and the horizontal strokes each represent two fingers.
  - **interpretation:** 扌 is a simplified form of 手 (shǒu, 'hand'), retaining the key elements that visually represent a human hand. It is commonly used as a component in other characters related to hand actions.
  - **simplification:** 扌 is derived as a cursive or shorthand form of 手 (shǒu, 'hand'), making it easier to incorporate into complex characters as a radical or component.
- **examples:**
  - 他伸出扌(手)接住了飞(飛)来(來)的球。
    - Tā shēnchū shǒu jiēzhù le fēilái de qiú.
    - He stretched out his hand to catch the flying ball.
  - 她用扌(手)制(製)作美丽(麗)的陶艺(藝)，展现(現)她的匠心。
    - Tā yòng shǒu zhìzuò měilì de táoyì, zhǎnxiàn tā de jiàngxīn.
    - She used her hand to create beautiful pottery, showcasing her craftsmanship.
  - 艺(藝)术(術)家细(細)心雕刻扌(手)的每一细(細)节(節)。
    - Yìshùjiā xìxīn diāokè shǒu de měiyī xìjié.
    - The artist meticulously carved every detail of the hand.
### 打听(聽) → 打 → 丁
- **definition:** fourth; robust
- **pinyin:** dīng
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts the head of a nail ->
    - 丁
  - **interpretation:** The character 丁 originally depicted the head of a nail, emphasizing simplicity and directness. While it has developed other interpretations over time, such as a head or city wall, these relate to similar shapes and functions. Today, 釘 (dīng, 'nail') reflects this meaning.
- **examples:**
  - 工人熟练(練)地把丁敲进(進)了墙(牆)壁。
    - Gōngrén shúliàn de bǎ dīng qiāng jìnle qiángbì.
    - The worker skillfully hammered the nail into the wall.
  - 他精心挑选(選)了铁(鐵)质(質)丁，确(確)保家(傢)具(俱)稳(穩)固。
    - Tā jīngxīn tiāoxuǎnle tiě zhì dīng, quèbǎo jiājù wěngù.
    - He carefully selected the iron nail to ensure the furniture was stable.
  - 请(請)把散落的丁收好。
    - Qǐng bǎ sànluò de dīng shōuhǎo.
    - Please gather the scattered nails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 丁](@media/glyph4e01.png)
### 打听(聽) → 聽
- **definition:** listen; hear
- **pinyin:** tīng
- **components:**
  - 耳
    - ěr
    - ear
  - 口
    - kǒu
    - mouth
  - 𡈼
    - unknown
    - unknown
  - 㥁
    - unknown
    - unknown
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - Originally 𦔻 ->
    - ideogrammic compound (耳 ('ear') + 口 ('mouths')) ->
    - Later as phono-semantic: phonetic 𡈼 + semantic 耳 ('ear') + semantic 㥁
  - **interpretation:** 聽(tīng, 'listen; hear') combines multiple elements related to the act of listening: 耳 (ěr, 'ear') represents the organ involved, while 𡈼 provides the phonetic cue. The additional semantic element 㥁 emphasizes the idea of focused attention or presence, completing the concept of listening carefully.
  - **simplification:** The traditional character 聽 was simplified to 听 by adopting the unrelated earlier character 𠯸, which was itself stylized and phoneticized in modern simplification processes.
- **examples:**
  - 我喜欢(歡)听(聽)音乐(樂)。
    - Wǒ xǐhuān tīng yīnyuè.
    - I like to listen to music.
  - 请(請)仔细(細)听(聽)讲(講)，保持安静(靜)。
    - Qǐng zǐxì tīngjiǎng，bǎochí ānjìng.
    - Please listen carefully and keep quiet.
  - 孩子们(們)坐下，安静(靜)地听(聽)故事。
    - Háizimen zuò xià，ānjìng de tīng gùshì.
    - The children sat down and listened quietly to the story.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 聽](@media/glyph807d.png)
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 耳
- **definition:** ear
- **pinyin:** ěr
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an ear
  - **interpretation:** The character 耳 (ěr, "ear") is a pictogram that visually represents an ear with its distinctive shape. This straightforward representation made it intuitive for ancient speakers to associate the character directly with the concept of an ear.
- **examples:**
  - 音乐(樂)直入耳。
    - Yīn yuè zhí rù ěr.
    - The music goes straight to the ear.
  - 他亲(親)耳听(聽)到谣(謠)言，心中充满(滿)疑虑(慮)。
    - Tā qīn ěr tīng dào yáo yán, xīn zhōng chōng mǎn yí lǜ.
    - He heard the rumor with his own ears, and his heart was filled with doubt.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 耳](@media/glyph8033.png)
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 口
- **definition:** mouth
- **pinyin:** kǒu
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an open mouth.
  - **interpretation:** The character 口(kǒu, 'mouth') is a straightforward pictogram that visually represents an open mouth. It is a fundamental character in the Chinese language, often used both as an independent word and as a component in more complex characters, lending a semantic association to ideas relating to speech, openings, or enclosures.
- **examples:**
  - 他张(張)开(開)口，大声(聲)喊叫。
    - Tā zhāngkāi kǒu, dàshēng hǎnjiào.
    - He opened his mouth and shouted loudly.
  - 这(這)口饭(飯)入口即化。
    - Zhè kǒu fàn rùkǒu jíhuà.
    - This mouthful of food melts in your mouth.
  - 小女孩咬了一口苹(蘋)果，露出甜美的笑容。
    - Xiǎo nǚhái yǎole yī kǒu píngguǒ, lùchū tiánměi de xiàoróng.
    - The little girl took a bite of the apple and smiled sweetly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 口](@media/glyph53e3.png)
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 𡈼
- **definition:** unknown
- **pinyin:** unknown
- **components:**
  - 亻
    - rén
    - person
  - 土
    - tǔ
    - soil
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** 亻(human) standing on 土(soil)
  - **interpretation:** The character depicts a human figure represented by 亻 standing upon the ground or soil, represented by 土, reflecting the concept of a person in relation to the earth.
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 𡈼 → 亻
- **definition:** person
- **pinyin:** rén
- **components:**
  - 人
    - rén
    - person
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Stylization of 人 (rén, "person") as a side radical to depict a person
  - **interpretation:** 亻 is a stylized form of 人 (rén, "person") used to indicate human-related meanings when combined with other components in characters as a radical. It visually represents a standing person, maintaining the core meaning of 'person' while facilitating the construction of complex characters.
- **examples:**
  - 他是一个(個)热(熱)心的人。
    - Tā shì yī gè rèxīn de rén.
    - He is a kind-hearted person.
  - 这(這)座城市里(裡)住着(著)很多优(優)秀的人。
    - Zhè zuò chéngshì lǐ zhùzhe hěn duō yōuxiù de rén.
    - There are many outstanding people living in this city.
  - 每个(個)人都有梦(夢)想。
    - Měi gè rén dōu yǒu mèngxiǎng.
    - Everyone has dreams.
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 𡈼 → 亻 → 人
- **definition:** person
- **pinyin:** rén
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:**
    - Depicts side view of a standing man, highlighting an arm and a leg ->
    - visual representation of a person
  - **interpretation:** The character 人 (rén, 'person') effectively uses simple lines to depict the essential form of a human, making it immediately recognizable and intuitive as meaning 'person.'
- **examples:**
  - 他是个(個)好人。
    - Tā shì gè hǎo rén.
    - He is a good person.
  - 每个(個)人都有责(責)任，为(為)社会(會)作出贡(貢)献(獻)。
    - Měi gè rén dōu yǒu zérèn, wèi shèhuì zuòchū gòngxiàn.
    - Every person has a responsibility to contribute to society.
  - 人在旅途中，心灵(靈)获(獲)得了成长(長)。
    - Rén zài lǚtú zhōng, xīnlíng huòdé le chéngzhǎng.
    - People gain growth along their journey.

### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 𡈼 → 土

- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a mound of earth
  - **interpretation:** The character 土(tǔ, "earth") visually represents a mound or piece of land, with a horizontal line indicating the surface and a vertical line the height of the mound. It's a straightforward depiction of earth or soil.
- **examples:**
  - 农(農)民耕土，种(種)出丰(豐)收。
    - Nóngmín gēng tǔ, zhòng chū fēngshōu.
    - Farmers cultivate the earth and harvest abundantly.
  - 院子里(裡)的土，适(適)合种(種)花。
    - Yuànzi lǐ de tǔ, shìhé zhòng huā.
    - The soil in the yard is suitable for planting flowers.

### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 㥁
- **definition:** unknown
- **pinyin:** unknown
- **components:**
  - 德
    - dé
    - virtue
  - 彳
    - chì
    - road
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** variant form
  - **description:** Variant of 德 (dé, "virtue")
  - **interpretation:** The character 㥁 is a variant form of 德 (dé, "virtue"), which combines semantic 彳 (chì, "road") indicating a path or method and phonetic 惪 (dé, "virtue") suggesting the sound. 德 implies following a path of moral integrity or virtue.
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 㥁 → 德
- **definition:** virtue
- **pinyin:** dé
- **components:**
  - 彳
    - chì
    - road
  - 惪
    - dé
    - virtue
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 彳 (chì, "road") + phonetic 惪 (dé, "virtue") ->
    - 德
  - **interpretation:** The character 德 (dé, "virtue") combines 彳 (chì, "road"), suggesting a path or way to follow, with the phonetic component 惪, which shares the virtue-related meaning. The road or path implies a moral journey or conduct, aligning with the concept of virtue as a way of life or code of behavior.
- **examples:**
  - 他的品德很好。
    - Tā de pǐndé hěn hǎo.
    - His virtue is very good.
  - 我们(們)应(應)该(該)学(學)习(習)孔子的道德思想。
    - Wǒmen yīnggāi xuéxí Kǒngzǐ de dàodé sīxiǎng.
    - We should study Confucius's moral philosophy.
  - 德行是一个(個)人真正的财(財)富。
    - Déxíng shì yīgè rén zhēnzhèng de cáifù.
    - Virtue is a person's true wealth.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 德](@media/glyph5fb7.png)
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 㥁 → 德 → 彳
- **definition:** road
- **pinyin:** chì
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a foot or person walking
  - **interpretation:** 彳(chì, 'walking') visually represents steps or a person moving, suggesting the idea of walking or movement. Despite a simplified history from characters like 行(xíng, 'walk'), its pictographic heritage directly connects with the notion of stepping or proceeding.
- **examples:**
  - 他喜欢(歡)在河边(邊)慢慢地走。
    - Tā xǐhuān zài hé biān mànmàn de zǒu.
    - He likes to walk slowly by the river.
  - 我们(們)每天退出喧嚣(囂)，享受安静(靜)的散步。
    - Wǒmen měitiān tuìchū xuānxiāo, xiǎngshòu ānjìng de sànbù.
    - We withdraw from the hustle and bustle every day to enjoy a quiet walk.
  - 他常常独(獨)自彳亍于(於)公园(園)小径(徑)。
    - Tā chángcháng dúzì chìchù yú gōngyuán xiǎojìng.
    - He often walks alone on the park trails.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 彳](@media/glyph5f73.png)
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 㥁 → 德 → 惪
- **definition:** virtue
- **pinyin:** dé
- **components:**
  - 直
    - zhí
    - looking forward
  - 心
    - xīn
    - heart
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** phono-semantic compound
  - **description:**
    - semantic 心 (xīn, "heart") + phonetic 直 (zhí, "looking forward") ->
    - virtue
  - **interpretation:** The character 惪(dé, "virtue") is formed with the semantic component 心 (xīn, "heart"), representing emotions or moral inclinations, combined with the phonetic component 直 (zhí, "looking forward"), indicating direction or straightness. The leading notion here is moral uprightness and sincerity, as a straight path represents honesty and virtue.
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 㥁 → 德 → 惪 → 直
- **definition:** looking forward
- **pinyin:** zhí
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts an eye above a horizontal line, originally representing 'straight' or 'upright.'
  - **interpretation:** The character 直 (zhí, 'straight') is a pictogram showing a vertical line beneath an eye at the top, imitating a straight path or direct sightline, symbolizing directness or straightforwardness.
- **examples:**
  - 她的头(頭)发(髮)很直。
    - Tā de tóufǎ hěn zhí.
    - Her hair is very straight.
  - 飞(飛)机(機)从(從)北京直飞(飛)，到达(達)东(東)京。
    - Fēijī cóng Běijīng zhífēi, dào dá Dōngjīng.
    - The airplane flies directly from Beijing to Tokyo.
  - 他直言不讳(諱)。
    - Tā zhí yán bù huì.
    - He speaks frankly.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 直](@media/glyph76f4.png)
### 打听(聽) → 聽 → 㥁 → 德 → 惪 → 心
- **definition:** heart
- **pinyin:** xīn
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** pictogram
  - **description:** Depicts a heart
  - **interpretation:** The character 心(xīn, "heart") originally depicted the shape of an actual heart, representing thoughts, emotions, and the core of a person. Over time, it has become highly stylized, but it continues to convey the notion of the heart as the center of emotions and consciousness.
- **examples:**
  - 她的心一直都在帮(幫)助别(別)人。
    - Tā de xīn yīzhí dōu zài bāngzhù biérén.
    - Her heart is always in helping others.
  - 在城市的中心，有一个(個)美丽(麗)的公园(園)。
    - Zài chéngshì de zhōngxīn, yǒu yí gè měilì de gōngyuán.
    - At the center of the city, there is a beautiful park.
  - 对(對)于(於)许(許)多人来(來)说(說)，家庭是生活的核心。
    - Duìyú xǔduō rén lái shuō, jiātíng shì shēnghuó de héxīn.
    - For many people, family is the core of life.
- **historical forms:**

![Historical forms of 心](@media/glyph5fc3.png)
